% Workflow for TYPES 2021 paper:
% 1. Edit/improve the literate Agda file `src/Demos/HSP.lagda`.
% 2. Invoke `agda --latex --latex-dir=doc/TYPES2021 src/Demos/HSP.lagda` from the main `agda-algebras` directory.
% 3. Invoke `pdflatex agda-hsp` from within the `doc/TYPES2021` directory.

\section{Introduction}
The Agda Universal Algebra Library (\agdaalgebras) \cite{ualib_v2.0.1} formalizes the foundations of universal algebra
in intensional Martin-LÃ¶f type theory (\mltt) using \agda~\cite{Norell:2007,agdaref}.
The library includes a collection of definitions and verified theorems originated in classical
(set-theory based) universal algebra and equational logic, but adapted to \mltt.

The first major milestone of the project is a complete formalization of \emph{Birkhoff's
variety theorem} (also known as the \emph{HSP theorem})~\cite{Birkhoff:1935}.
To the best of our knowledge, this is the first time Birkhoff's celebrated 1935 result
has been formalized in \mltt.\footnote{An alternative formalization based on classical
set-theory was achieved in~\cite{birkhoff-in-mizar:1999}.}
%; see \href{http://www.mizar.org/JFM/Vol9/birkhoff.html\#BIB21}{mizar.org/JFM/Vol9/birkhoff.html}.}

Our first attempt to formalize Birkhoff's theorem
suffered from two flaws.\footnote{See the
 \href{https://github.com/ualib/ualib.github.io/blob/71f173858701398d56224dd79d152c380c0c2b5e/src/lagda/UALib/Birkhoff.lagda}{\textsf{Birkhoff.lagda}} file
 in the \href{https://github.com/ualib/ualib.github.io}{\textsf{ualib/ualib.gitlab.io}}
 repository (\href{https://github.com/ualib/ualib.github.io/commit/71f173858701398d56224dd79d152c380c0c2b5e}{15
 Jan 2021 commit 71f1738})~\cite{ualib_v1.0.0}.}
First, we assumed function extensionality in \mltt; consequently, it was unclear whether the formalization was fully constructive.  Second, an inconsistency could be
contrived by taking the type \ab{X}, representing an arbitrary collection of
variable symbols, to be the two element type (see Â§\ref{sec:discuss} for details).  To resolve these issues, we developed a new formalization of the HSP theorem based on \textit{setoids} and rewrote much of the \agdaalgebras library to support this approach.  This enabled us to avoid function extensionality altogether.  Moreover, the type \ab{X} of variable symbols was treated with more care using the \textit{context} and \textit{environment} types that Andreas Abel uses in~\cite{Abel:2021} to formalize Birkhoff's completeness theorem. These design choices are discussed further in Â§\ref{setoids}--\ref{setoid-functions}.

What follows is a self-contained formal proof of the HSP theorem in \agda.
%\footnote{The proof presented here is based on \agdaalgebras, ver.~2.0.1~\cite{ualib_v2.0.1}, \agda ver.2.6.2 a%nd \agdastdlib ver.1.7.}
%is constructive and correct.
This is achieved by
extracting a subset of the \agdaalgebras library, including only the
pieces needed for the proof, into a single literate \agda file.\footnote{%
\HSPlagda in the \agdaalgebras repository: \agdaalgebrasrepo}
\ifshort %%% BEGIN SHORT VERSION ONLY
For spaces reasons, we elide some inessential parts,
but strive to preserve the essential content and character of the development.
Specifically, routine or overly technical components, as well as anything that does not
seem to offer insight into the central ideas of the proof are omitted. (The file \HSPlagda mentioned above includes the full proof.)
%can be found in the file \HSPlagda in the \agdaalgebras repository.}
%or in the unabridged version of the present paper~\cite{DeMeo:2021}.}
       %%% END SHORT VERSION ONLY
\else  %%% BEGIN LONG VERSION ONLY
We include here every line of code of our new proof of Birkhoff's theorem
in a single \agda module, presented as a literate \agda document,\footnote{See
\HSPlagda in the \agdaalgebras repository: \agdaalgebrasrepo .}.  Apart from a few dozen
imports from the \agdastdlib, the module is self-contained.
\fi

In this paper, we highlight some of the more challenging aspects of formalizing universal algebra in type theory.  To some extent, this is a sobering glimpse of the significant technical hurdles that must be overcome to do mathematics in dependent type theory. Nonetheless, we hope to demonstrate that \mltt is a relatively natural language for formalizing universal algebra.  Indeed, we believe that researchers with sufficient patience and resolve can reap the substantial rewards of deeper insight and greater confidence in their results by using type theory and a proof assistant like \agda.
On the other hand, this paper is probably not the best place to learn about the latter, since we assume the reader is already familiar with \mltt and \agda.
In summary, our main contribution is to show that a straightforward but very general representation of algebraic structures in dependent type theory is quite practical, as we demonstrate by formalizing a major seminal result of universal algebra.

\section{Preliminaries}

\subsection{Logical foundations}

To best emulate \mltt, we use
<pre class="Agda">
<a id="5052" class="Symbol">{-#</a> <a id="5056" class="Keyword">OPTIONS</a> <a id="5064" class="Pragma">--without-K</a> <a id="5076" class="Pragma">--exact-split</a> <a id="5090" class="Pragma">--safe</a> <a id="5097" class="Symbol">#-}</a>
</pre>
;
\ifshort  %%% BEGIN SHORT VERSION ONLY
  \AgdaPragma{without-K} disables
  \href{https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/axiom+K+%28type+theory%29}{Streicher's K axiom};
  \AgdaPragma{exact-split} directs \agda to accept only definitions behaving like
  {\it judgmental} equalities;
  \AgdaPragma{safe} ensures that nothing is postulated outright.
  (See~\cite{agdaref-axiomk,agdaref-safeagda,agdatools-patternmatching}.)
       %%% END SHORT VERSION ONLY
\else  %%% BEGIN LONG VERSION ONLY

  Here are brief descriptions of these options, accompanied by links to related documentation.
  \begin{itemize}
  \item
  \AgdaPragma{without-K} disables \href{https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/axiom+K+%28type+theory%29}{Streicher's K axiom}.
  See the \href{https://agda.readthedocs.io/en/v2.6.1/language/without-k.html}{section on axiom K} in
  the \href{https://agda.readthedocs.io/en/v2.6.1.3/language}{Agda Language Reference Manual}~\cite{agdaref-axiomk}.
  \item
  \AgdaPragma{exact-split} makes \agda accept only those definitions that behave like so-called {\it judgmental} equalities.
  See the \href{https://agda.readthedocs.io/en/v2.6.1/tools/command-line-options.html#pattern-matching-and-equality}%
  {Pattern matching and equality} section of
  the \href{https://agda.readthedocs.io/en/v2.6.1.3/tools/}{Agda Tools} documentation~\cite{agdatools-patternmatching}.
  \item
  \AgdaPragma{safe} ensures that nothing is postulated outright---every non-\mltt axiom has to be an explicit assumption (e.g., an argument to a function or module).
  See the \href{https://agda.readthedocs.io/en/v2.6.1/tools/command-line-options.html#cmdoption-safe}{cmdoption-safe} section of~\cite{agdaref-safeagda}.
  \end{itemize}
\fi    %%% END LONG VERSION ONLY
We also make use of the following definitions from \agda's standard library (ver.~1.7).

</pre>

</pre>
}
\noindent The above imports include some adjustments to ``standard'' \agda syntax; in particular,
we use \AgdaPrimitive{Type} in place of \AgdaPrimitive{Set}, the infix long arrow symbol,
\AgdaRecord{\AgdaUnderscore{}âŸ¶\AgdaUnderscore{}}, in place of \AgdaRecord{Func} (the type of ``setoid functions,'' discussed in Â§\ref{setoid-functions} below), and the symbol \aofld{\au{}âŸ¨\$âŸ©\au{}} in place of \afld{f} (application of the map of a setoid function); we use
\AgdaField{fst} and \AgdaField{snd}, and sometimes \AgdaOperator{\AgdaFunction{âˆ£\AgdaUnderscore{}âˆ£}} and
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaFunction{âˆ¥\AgdaUnderscore{}âˆ¥}}, to denote the first and second
projections out of the product type
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaFunction{\AgdaUnderscore{}Ã—\AgdaUnderscore{}}}.
\ifshort
\else  %%% BEGIN LONG VERSION ONLY

<pre class="Agda">

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Setoids}\label{setoids}
A \defn{setoid} is a pair consisting of a type and
an equivalence relation on that type.  Setoids are useful for representing a
set with an explicit, ``local'' notion of equivalence, instead of relying on
an implicit, ``global'' one as is more common in set theory. In reality,
informal mathematical practice relies on equivalence relations quite pervasively,
taking great care to define only functions that preserve equivalences, while eliding the
details. To be properly formal, such details must be made explicit.
While there are many different workable approaches, the one that requires
no additional meta-theory is based on setoids, which is why we adopt it here.
While in some settings setoids are found by others to be burdensome, we have not
found them to be so for universal algebra.

The \agdaalgebras library was first developed without setoids, relying on
propositional equality %\ad{\au{}â‰¡\au{}}
instead,
along with some experimental, domain-specific types for equivalence classes, quotients, etc.
This required postulating function extensionality,%
\footnote{the axiom asserting that two point-wise equal functions are equal} which is
known to be independent from \mltt~\cite{MHE, MHE:2019}; this was unsatisfactory as %we were curious to see if
we aimed to show that the theorems hold directly in \mltt without extra axioms.
The present work makes no appeal to functional extensionality or classical axioms like Choice or Excluded Middle.\footnote{All submodules of the \am{Setoid} module in the \agdaalgebras library are also fully constructive in this sense.}


%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Setoid functions}
\label{setoid-functions}
A \textit{setoid function} is a function from
one setoid to another that respects the underlying equivalences.
If \ab{ğ‘¨} and \ab{ğ‘©} are setoids, we use \ab{ğ‘¨}~\AgdaRecord{âŸ¶}~\ab{ğ‘©}
to denote the type of setoid functions from \ab{ğ‘¨} to \ab{ğ‘©}.
\ifshort
\else %%% BEGIN LONG VERSION ONLY

An example of a setoid function is the identity function from a setoid to itself.
We define it, along with a binary composition operation for setoid functions,
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaFunction{âŸ¨âˆ˜âŸ©}}, as follows.

\paragraph*{Inverses}
\fi %%% END LONG VERSION ONLY
We define the \defn{inverse} of such a function in terms of the image of the function's domain, as follows.

</pre>

An inhabitant of the \aod{Image} \ab f \aod{âˆ‹} \ab b type is a point \ab a~\as :~\afld{Carrier}\ab{ğ‘¨},
along with a proof \ab p~\as :~\ab b~\af{â‰ˆ}~\ab f~\ab a, that \ab f maps \ab a to \ab b.
Since a proof of \aod{Image} \ab f \aod{âˆ‹} \ab b must include a concrete witness \ab a~\as :~\afld{Carrier}~\ab{ğ‘¨}, we can actually \emph{compute} a range-restricted right-inverse of \ab f.
Here is the definition of \af{Inv} which, for extra certainty, is accompanied by a proof that it gives a right-inverse.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="14039" href="Demos.HSP.html#14039" class="Function">Inv</a> <a id="14043" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14045" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14046" href="Demos.HSP.html#14046" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14048" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14050" href="Demos.HSP.html#13300" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="14052" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="14054" href="Demos.HSP.html#13317" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a><a id="14055" class="Symbol">){</a><a id="14057" href="Demos.HSP.html#14057" class="Bound">b</a> <a id="14059" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14061" href="Demos.HSP.html#13397" class="Field">B</a><a id="14062" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="14064" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="14066" href="Demos.HSP.html#13408" class="Datatype Operator">Image</a> <a id="14072" href="Demos.HSP.html#14046" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14074" href="Demos.HSP.html#13408" class="Datatype Operator">âˆ‹</a> <a id="14076" href="Demos.HSP.html#14057" class="Bound">b</a> <a id="14078" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="14080" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1072" class="Field">Carrier</a> <a id="14088" href="Demos.HSP.html#13300" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a>
 <a id="14091" href="Demos.HSP.html#14039" class="Function">Inv</a> <a id="14095" class="Symbol">_</a> <a id="14097" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14098" href="Demos.HSP.html#13461" class="InductiveConstructor">eq</a> <a id="14101" href="Demos.HSP.html#14101" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="14103" class="Symbol">_)</a> <a id="14106" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="14108" href="Demos.HSP.html#14101" class="Bound">a</a>

 <a id="14112" href="Demos.HSP.html#14112" class="Function">InvIsInverseÊ³</a> <a id="14126" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14128" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="14129" href="Demos.HSP.html#14129" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14131" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14133" href="Demos.HSP.html#13300" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="14135" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="14137" href="Demos.HSP.html#13317" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a><a id="14138" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="14140" href="Demos.HSP.html#14140" class="Bound">b</a> <a id="14142" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14144" href="Demos.HSP.html#13397" class="Field">B</a><a id="14145" class="Symbol">}(</a><a id="14147" href="Demos.HSP.html#14147" class="Bound">q</a> <a id="14149" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14151" href="Demos.HSP.html#13408" class="Datatype Operator">Image</a> <a id="14157" href="Demos.HSP.html#14129" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14159" href="Demos.HSP.html#13408" class="Datatype Operator">âˆ‹</a> <a id="14161" href="Demos.HSP.html#14140" class="Bound">b</a><a id="14162" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14164" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="14166" href="Demos.HSP.html#14129" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14168" href="Demos.HSP.html#8608" class="Field Operator">âŸ¨$âŸ©</a> <a id="14172" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14173" href="Demos.HSP.html#14039" class="Function">Inv</a> <a id="14177" href="Demos.HSP.html#14129" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14179" href="Demos.HSP.html#14147" class="Bound">q</a><a id="14180" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14182" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1098" class="Field Operator">â‰ˆ</a> <a id="14184" href="Demos.HSP.html#14140" class="Bound">b</a>
 <a id="14187" href="Demos.HSP.html#14112" class="Function">InvIsInverseÊ³</a> <a id="14201" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14202" href="Demos.HSP.html#13461" class="InductiveConstructor">eq</a> <a id="14205" class="Symbol">_</a> <a id="14207" href="Demos.HSP.html#14207" class="Bound">p</a><a id="14208" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14210" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="14212" href="Relation.Binary.Structures.html#1594" class="Function">sym</a> <a id="14216" href="Demos.HSP.html#14207" class="Bound">p</a>
</pre>
%
\ifshort\else
\paragraph*{Injective and surjective setoid functions}
\fi

If \ab{f} : \ab{ğ‘¨} \aor{âŸ¶} \ab{ğ‘©}
then we call \ab f \defn{injective} provided
\as{âˆ€}(\ab{aâ‚€} \ab{aâ‚} \as : \ab{A}), \ab{f}~\aofld{âŸ¨\$âŸ©}~\ab{aâ‚€}~\af{â‰ˆá´®}~\ab{f}~\aofld{âŸ¨\$âŸ©}~\ab{aâ‚}
implies \ab{aâ‚€}~\af{â‰ˆá´¬}~\ab{aâ‚}; we call \ab{f} \defn{surjective} provided
\as{âˆ€}(\AgdaTyped{b}{B})~\as{âˆƒ}(\AgdaTyped{a}{A}) such that \ab{f} \aofld{âŸ¨\$âŸ©} \ab{a} \af{â‰ˆá´®} \ab{b}.
\ifshort
We omit the straightforward \agda definitions.
\else

We represent injective functions on bare types by the
type \af{Injective}, and uses this to define the \af{IsInjective} type to represent
the property of being an injective setoid function. Similarly, the type \af{IsSurjective}
represents the property of being a surjective setoid function. \af{SurjInv} represents the \emph{right-inverse} of a surjective function.

We reproduce the definitions and prove some of their properties
inside the next submodule where we first set the stage by declaring two
setoids \ab{ğ‘¨} and \ab{ğ‘©}, naming their equality relations, and making some
definitions from the standard library available.

</pre>

Proving that the composition of injective setoid functions is again injective
is simply a matter of composing the two assumed witnesses to injectivity.
Proving that surjectivity is preserved under composition is only slightly more involved.

<pre class="Agda">

\paragraph*{Factorization of setoid functions\protect\footnote{The code in this paragraph was suggested by an anonymous referee.}}

Any (setoid) function \ab f : \ab A \aor{âŸ¶} \ab B factors as a surjective map
\ab{toIm} : \ab A \aor{âŸ¶} \ab{Im} \ab f followed by an injective map \ab{fromIm} : \ab{Im} \ab f \aor{âŸ¶} \ab B.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="16993" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="17000" href="Demos.HSP.html#17000" class="Module">_</a> <a id="17002" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="17003" href="Demos.HSP.html#17003" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="17005" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17007" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1009" class="Record">Setoid</a> <a id="17014" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="17016" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a><a id="17018" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="17020" href="Demos.HSP.html#17020" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="17022" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17024" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1009" class="Record">Setoid</a> <a id="17031" href="Demos.HSP.html#9445" class="Generalizable">Î²</a> <a id="17033" href="Demos.HSP.html#9447" class="Generalizable">Ïáµ‡</a><a id="17035" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="17037" class="Keyword">where</a>

%\paragraph*{Kernels of setoid functions}
%The \defn{kernel} of a function \ab f~\as :~\ab A~\as{â†’}~\ab B is defined informally by \{\AgdaPair{x}{y} \aod{âˆˆ} \ab A \aof{Ã—} \ab A \as : \ab f \ab x \as{=} \ab f \ab y\}. This can be represented in a number of ways, but for our purposes it is convenient to define the kernel as an inhabitant of a (unary) predicate over \ab A \aof{Ã—} \ab A.

%% -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

\section{Basic Universal Algebra}
\label{basic-universal-algebra}
We now develop a working vocabulary in \mltt corresponding to classical,
single-sorted, set-based universal algebra.
We cover a number of important concepts, but limit ourselves to those
required to prove Birkhoff's HSP theorem.
%\footnote{The concepts we formalize here are just a fraction of those formalized in the \agdaalgebras library.}
In each case, we give a type-theoretic version of the informal definition,
followed by its \agda implementation.

This section is organized into the following subsections:
Â§\ref{signatures} defines a general type of \emph{signatures} of algebraic structures;
Â§\ref{algebras} does the same for structures and their products;
Â§\ref{homomorphisms} defines \emph{homomorphisms}, \emph{monomorphisms}, and \emph{epimorphisms},
presents types that codify these concepts, and formally verifies some of their basic properties;
Â§\ref{subalgebras}--\ref{terms} do the same for \emph{subalgebras} and \emph{terms}, respectively.

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Signatures}
\label{signatures}

\ifshort
An (algebraic) \defn{signature}
\else
In model theory, the \defn{signature} of a structure is a quadruple \ab{ğ‘†} = (\ab{C},
\ab{F}, \ab{R}, \ab{Ï}) consisting of three (possibly empty) sets \ab{C}, \ab{F}, and
\ab{R}---called \emph{constant}, \emph{function}, and \emph{relation} symbols,
respectively---along with a function \ab{Ï} : \ab{C} \as{+} \ab{F} \as{+} \ab{R}
\as{â†’} \ab{N} that assigns an \emph{arity} to each symbol. Often, but not always, \ab{N}
is taken to be the set of natural numbers.

As our focus here is universal algebra, we consider the restricted notion of an
\emph{algebraic signature}, that is, a signature for ``purely algebraic'' structures. Such
a signature
\fi
is a pair \ab{ğ‘†} = \AgdaPair{F}{Ï} where \ab{F} is a collection of
\defn{operation symbols} and \ab{Ï} : \ab{F} \as{â†’} \ab{N} is an \defn{arity function}
which maps each operation symbol to its arity. Here, \ab{N} denotes the \emph{arity type}.
Heuristically, the arity \ab{Ï} \ab{f} of an operation symbol \ab{f} \aof{âˆˆ} \ab{F} may be
thought of as the number of arguments that \ab{f} takes as ``input.''
%Here (and in the \agdaalgebras library) w
We represent signatures as inhabitants of the following dependent pair type.

\begin{center}

\AgdaFunction{Signature}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaBound{ğ“}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{ğ“¥}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaPostulate{Level}\AgdaSymbol{)}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{â†’}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaPrimitive{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaPrimitive{lsuc}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaBound{ğ“}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaPrimitive{âŠ”}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{ğ“¥}\AgdaSymbol{))}\\[4pt]
\AgdaFunction{Signature}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{ğ“}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{ğ“¥}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{=}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaFunction{Î£[}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{F}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaFunction{âˆˆ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaPrimitive{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{ğ“}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaFunction{]}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaBound{F}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{â†’}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaPrimitive{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{ğ“¥}\AgdaSymbol{)}

\end{center}
Recalling our syntax for the first and second
projections, if \ab{ğ‘†} %\as{:} \af{Signature} \ab{ğ“} \ab{ğ“¥}
is a signature, then
\aof{âˆ£} \ab{ğ‘†} \aof{âˆ£} denotes the set of operation symbols and \aof{âˆ¥} \ab{ğ‘†} \aof{âˆ¥} denotes the arity function.
Thus, if \ab{f} \as{:} \aof{âˆ£} \ab{ğ‘†} \aof{âˆ£} is an operation symbol in the
signature \ab{ğ‘†}, then \aof{âˆ¥} \ab{ğ‘†} \aof{âˆ¥} \ab{f} is the arity of \ab{f}.

We need to augment our \af{Signature} type so that it supports algebras over setoid domains.
To do so, following Abel~\cite{Abel:2021}, we
define an operator that translates an ordinary signature into a \defn{setoid signature},
that is, a signature over a setoid domain.
This raises a minor technical issue:
given operations \ab{f} and \ab{g}, with arguments
\ab{u}~\as{:}~\aof{âˆ¥}~\ab{ğ‘†}~\aof{âˆ¥}~\ab{f}~\as{â†’}~\ab{A} and \ab{v}~\as{:}~\aof{âˆ¥}~\ab{ğ‘†}~\aof{âˆ¥}~\ab{g}~\as{â†’}~\ab{A}, respectively, and a proof of \ab{f}~\aod{â‰¡}~\ab{g} (\textit{intensional} equality), we ought to be able to check whether \ab u and \ab v are pointwise
equal. Technically, \ab{u} and \ab{v} appear to inhabit different types; of course, this is reconciled by the hypothesis \ab f \aod{â‰¡} \ab g, as we see in the next definition (borrowed
from~\cite{Abel:2021}).

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="EqArgs"></a><a id="22599" href="Demos.HSP.html#22599" class="Function">EqArgs</a> <a id="22606" class="Symbol">:</a>  <a id="22609" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="22610" href="Demos.HSP.html#22610" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a> <a id="22612" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="22614" href="Base.Algebras.Basic.html#3890" class="Function">Signature</a> <a id="22624" href="Demos.HSP.html#7259" class="Bound">ğ“</a> <a id="22626" href="Demos.HSP.html#7261" class="Bound">ğ“¥</a><a id="22627" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="22629" href="Demos.HSP.html#22629" class="Bound">Î¾</a> <a id="22631" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="22633" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1009" class="Record">Setoid</a> <a id="22640" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="22642" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a><a id="22644" class="Symbol">}</a>
 <a id="22647" class="Symbol">â†’</a>        <a id="22656" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="22658" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="22659" href="Demos.HSP.html#22659" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="22661" <a id="22698" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="22699" href="Demos.HSP.html#10401" class="Function Operator">âˆ¥</a> <a id="22701" href="Demos.HSP.html#22610" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a> <a id="22703" href="Demos.HSP.html#10401" class="Function Operator">âˆ¥</a> <a id="22705" href="Demos.HSP.html#22661" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="22707" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="22709" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1072" class="Field">Carrier</a> <a id="22717" href="Demos.HSP.html#22629" class="Bound">Î¾</a><a id="22718" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="22720" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="22722" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="22727" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="22728" href="Demos.HSP.html#7261" class="Bound">ğ“¥</a> <a id="22730" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="22732" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a><a id="22734" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="22736" href="Demos.HSP.html#22599" class="Function">EqArgs</a> <a id="22743" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="22744" class="Argument">Î¾</a> <a id="22746" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="22748" href="Demos.HSP.html#22748" class="Bound">Î¾</a><a id="22749" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="22751" href="Agda.Builtin.Equality.html#208" class="InductiveConstructor">â‰¡.refl</a> <a id="22758" href="Demos.HSP.html#22758" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="22760" href="Demos.HSP.html#22760" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="22762" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="22764" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="22766" href="Demos.HSP.html#22766" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="22768" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="22770" href="Demos.HSP.html#22758" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="22772" href="Demos.HSP.html#22766" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="22774" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1098" class="Function Operator">â‰ˆ</a> <a id="22776" href="Demos.HSP.html#22760" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="22778" href="Demos.HSP.html#22766" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="22780" class="Keyword">where</a> <a id="22786" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="22791" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1009" class="Module">Setoid</a> <a id="22798" href="Demos.HSP.html#22748" class="Bound">Î¾</a> <a id="22800" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="22806" class="Symbol">(</a> <a id="22808" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1098" class="Field Operator">_â‰ˆ_</a> <a id="22812" class="Symbol">)</a>

</pre>
\noindent
This makes it possible to define an operator which translates a signature for algebras over bare types into a signature for algebras over setoids.
We denote this operator by \aof{âŸ¨\AgdaUnderscore{}âŸ©}%
\ifshort
.
\else
 and define it as follows.
\fi

<pre class="Agda">

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Algebras}\label{algebras}
An \defn{algebraic structure} \ab{ğ‘¨} = (\ab{A}, \ab{Fá´¬}) \defn{in the signature}
\ab{ğ‘†} = (\ab{F}, \ab{Ï}), or \ab{ğ‘†}-\defn{algebra}, consists of
\begin{itemize}
\item a type \ab A, called the \defn{domain} of the algebra;
\item a collection \ab{Fá´¬} :=
  \{ \ab{fá´¬} \as{âˆ£} \ab f \aof{âˆˆ} \ab F, \ab{fá´¬} \as :
    (\ab{Ï} \ab f \as{â†’} \ab A) \as{â†’} \ab A \} of \defn{operations} on \ab{A};
\item a (potentially empty) collection of \defn{identities} satisfied by elements and
operations of \ab{ğ‘¨}.
\end{itemize}
Our \agda implementation represents algebras as inhabitants of a record type with two
fields---a \afld{Domain} setoid denoting the domain of the algebra, and an \afld{Interp} function denoting the interpretation in the algebra of each operation symbol in \ab{ğ‘†}. We postpone introducing identities until~Â§\ref{equational-logic}.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="24562" class="Keyword">record</a> <a id="Algebra"></a><a id="24569" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="24577" href="Demos.HSP.html#24577" class="Bound">Î±</a> <a id="24579" href="Demos.HSP.html#24579" class="Bound">Ï</a> <a id="24581" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="24583" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="24588" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="24589" href="Demos.HSP.html#7259" class="Bound">ğ“</a> <a id="24591" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="24593" href="Demos.HSP.html#7261" class="Bound">ğ“¥</a> <a id="24595" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="24597" href="Agda.Primitive.html#780" class="Primitive">lsuc</a> <a id="24602" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="24603" href="Demos.HSP.html#24577" class="Bound">Î±</a> <a id="24605" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="24607" href="Demos.HSP.html#24579" class="Bound">Ï</a><a id="24608" class="Symbol">))</a> <a id="24611" class="Keyword">where</a>
 <a id="24618" class="Keyword">field</a>  <a id="Algebra.Domain"></a><a id="24625" href="Demos.HSP.html#24625" class="Field">Domain</a>  <a id="24633" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="24635" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1009" class="Record">Setoid</a> <a id="24642" href="Demos.HSP.html#24577" class="Bound">Î±</a> <a id="24644" href="Demos.HSP.html#24579" class="Bound">Ï</a>
        <a id="Algebra.Interp"></a><a id="24654" href="Demos.HSP.html#24654" class="Field">Interp</a>  <a id="24662" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="24664" href="Demos.HSP.html#23100" class="Function Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="24666" href="Demos.HSP.html#7245" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a> <a id="24668" href="Demos.HSP.html#23100" class="Function Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="24670" href="Demos.HSP.html#24625" class="Field">Domain</a> <a id="24677" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="24679" href="Demos.HSP.html#24625" class="Field">Domain</a>

</pre>
Thus, for each operation symbol in \ab{ğ‘†} we have a setoid function
\ab f whose domain is a power of \afld{Domain} and whose codomain is \afld{Domain}.
Further, we define some syntactic sugar to make our formalizations easier to read and reason about. Specifically, if \ab{ğ‘¨} is an algebra, then
\begin{itemize}
\item \aof{ğ”»[ \ab{ğ‘¨} ]} denotes the \afld{Domain} setoid of \ab{ğ‘¨},
\item \aof{ğ•Œ[ \ab{ğ‘¨} ]} is the underlying carrier of (the \afld{Domain} setoid of) \ab{ğ‘¨}, and
\item \ab f \aof{Ì‚} \ab{ğ‘¨} denotes the interpretation of the operation symbol \ab f in the algebra \ab{ğ‘¨}.
\end{itemize}
\ifshort %%% BEGIN SHORT VERSION ONLY
 We omit the straightforward formal definitions (\seemedium).
\else    %%% END SHORT VERSION ONLY
         %%% BEGIN LONG VERSION ONLY SECTION
<pre class="Agda">

<a id="_Ì‚_"></a><a id="25612" href="Demos.HSP.html#25612" class="Function Operator">_Ì‚_</a> <a id="25616" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="25618" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25619" href="Demos.HSP.html#25619" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="25621" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="25623" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a> <a id="25625" href="Demos.HSP.html#7245" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a> <a id="25627" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a><a id="25628" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="25630" href="Demos.HSP.html#25630" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="25632" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="25634" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="25642" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="25644" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a><a id="25646" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="25648" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="25650" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25651" href="Demos.HSP.html#10401" class="Function Operator">âˆ¥</a> <a id="25653" href="Demos.HSP.html#7245" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a> <a id="25655" href="Demos.HSP.html#10401" class="Function Operator">âˆ¥</a> <a id="25657" href="Demos.HSP.html#25619" class="Bound">f</a>  <a id="25660" class="Symbol">â†’</a>  <a id="25663" href="Demos.HSP.html#25554" class="Function Operator">ğ•Œ[</a> <a id="25666" href="Demos.HSP.html#25630" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="25668" href="Demos.HSP.html#25554" class="Function Operator">]</a><a id="25669" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="25671" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="25673" href="Demos.HSP.html#25554" class="Function Operator">ğ•Œ[</a> <a id="25676" href="Demos.HSP.html#25630" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="25678" href="Demos.HSP.html#25554" class="Function Operator">]</a>

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\paragraph*{Universe levels of algebra types}
Types belong to \emph{universes}, which are structured in \agda as
follows:
\ap{Type} \ab{â„“} : \ap{Type} (\ap{suc} \ab{â„“}), \ap{Type} (\ap{suc} \ab{â„“}) : \ap{Type}
(\ap{suc} (\ap{suc} \ab{â„“})), â€¦.\footnote{\ap{suc} \ab{â„“} denotes the successor of \ab{â„“} in the universe hierarchy.} While this means that \ap{Type} \ab{â„“} has type \ap{Type}
(\ap{suc} \ab{â„“}), it does \emph{not} imply that \ap{Type} \ab{â„“} has type
\ap{Type} (\ap{suc} (\ap{suc} \ab{â„“})). In other words, \agda's universes are
\emph{non-cumulative}.
This can be advantageous as it becomes possible to treat size issues
more generally and precisely.  However, dealing with explicit
universe levels can be daunting, and the standard literature
(in which uniform smallness is typically assumed) offers little guidance.
\ifshort\else
This aspect of the language was one of the few stumbling
blocks we encountered while learning how to use \agda for formalizing universal algebra in
type theory. Although some may consider this to be one of the least interesting and most
technical aspects of this paper, others might find the presentation more helpful if we
resist the urge to gloss over these technicalities.
\fi
While in some settings, such as category theory, formalizing in \agda
works smoothly with respect to universe levels (see~\cite{agda-categories}), in universal algebra the
terrain is bumpier.
Thus, it seems worthwhile to explain how we make use
of universe lifting and lowering functions, available in the \agdastdlib, to
develop domain-specific tools for dealing with \agda's non-cumulative universe hierarchy.

\ifshort\else
Let us be more concrete about what is at issue by considering a typical example. \agda
frequently encounters problems during the type-checking process and responds by printing a
message like the following.
{\color{red}{\small
\begin{verbatim}
  HSP.lagda:498,20-23
  Î± != ğ“ âŠ” ğ“¥ âŠ” (lsuc Î±) when checking that... has type...
\end{verbatim}}}
\noindent Here \agda informs us that it encountered universe level \ab{Î±} on line 498 of
the HSP module, where it was expecting level \ab{ğ“}~\aop{âŠ”}~\ab{ğ“¥}~\aop{âŠ”}~(\ap{lsuc}
\ab{Î±}). In this case, we tried to use an algebra inhabiting the type \ar{Algebra}
\ab{Î±} \ab{Ïáµƒ} whereas \agda expected an inhabitant of the type \ar{Algebra} (\ab{ğ“}
\aop{âŠ”} \ab{ğ“¥} \aop{âŠ”} (\ap{lsuc} \ab{Î±})) \ab{Ïáµƒ}.
\fi
The \ar{Lift} operation of the standard library embeds a type into a higher universe.
Specializing \ar{Lift} to our situation, we
define a function \af{Lift-Alg}%
\ifshort
~with the following interface.
\vskip-2mm
\else
.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="Lift-Alg"></a><a id="29484" href="Demos.HSP.html#29484" class="Function">Lift-Alg</a> <a id="29493" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="29495" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="29503" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="29505" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a> <a id="29508" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="29510" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29511" href="Demos.HSP.html#29511" class="Bound">â„“â‚€</a> <a id="29514" href="Demos.HSP.html#29514" class="Bound">â„“â‚</a> <a id="29517" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="29519" href="Agda.Primitive.html#597" class="Postulate">Level</a><a id="29524" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="29526" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="29528" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="29536" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29537" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="29539" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="29541" href="Demos.HSP.html#29511" class="Bound">â„“â‚€</a><a id="29543" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="29545" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29546" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a> <a id="29549" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="29551" href="Demos.HSP.html#29514" class="Bound">â„“â‚</a><a id="29553" class="Symbol">)</a>
</pre>
\ifshort
\vskip2mm
\else
<pre class="Agda">
<a id="29604" href="Demos.HSP.html#29484" class="Function">Lift-Alg</a> <a id="29613" href="Demos.HSP.html#29613" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="29615" href="Demos.HSP.html#29615" class="Bound">â„“â‚€</a> <a id="29618" href="Demos.HSP.html#29618" class="Bound">â„“â‚</a> <a id="29621" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="29623" href="Demos.HSP.html#28938" class="Function">Lift-AlgÊ³</a> <a id="29633" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29634" href="Demos.HSP.html#28543" class="Function">Lift-AlgË¡</a> <a id="29644" href="Demos.HSP.html#29613" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="29646" href="Demos.HSP.html#29615" class="Bound">â„“â‚€</a><a id="29648" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="29650" href="Demos.HSP.html#29618" class="Bound">â„“â‚</a>

</pre>
\noindent Recall that our \ar{Algebra} type has two universe level parameters, corresponding
to those of the domain setoid.
Concretely, an algebra of type \ar{Algebra} \ab{Î±} \ab{Ïáµƒ} has a
\afld{Domain} of type \ar{Setoid} \ab{Î±} \ab{Ïáµƒ}. This packages a ``carrier set''
(\afld{Carrier}), inhabiting \ap{Type} \ab{Î±}, with an equality on \afld{Carrier} of type
\af{Rel} \afld{Carrier} \ab{Ïáµƒ}.
\fi
\noindent \af{Lift-Alg} takes an algebra parametrized by levels \ab{a} and \ab{Ïáµƒ}
and constructs a new algebra whose carrier inhabits \ap{Type} (\ab{Î±} \ap{âŠ”} \ab{â„“â‚€}) and
whose equivalence inhabits \af{Rel}~\afld{Carrier}~(\ab{Ïáµƒ}~\ap{âŠ”}~\ab{â„“â‚}).
To be useful, this lifting operation should result in an algebra with the same semantic properties
as the one we started with. We will see in Â§\ref{sec:lift-alg} that this is indeed the case.

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\paragraph*{Product Algebras}
We define the \defn{product} of a family of algebras as follows.
Let \ab{Î¹} be a universe and \ab I~:~\ap{Type}~\ab{Î¹} a type (the ``indexing type'').
Then \ab{ğ’œ}~:~\ab I~\as{â†’}~\ab{Algebra}~\ab{Î±}~\ab{Ïáµƒ} represents
an \defn{indexed family of algebras}.
Denote by \af{â¨…}~\ab{ğ’œ} the \defn{product of algebras} in \ab{ğ’œ} (or \defn{product
algebra}), by which we mean the algebra whose domain is the Cartesian product \af{Î }~\ab
i~ê‰~\ab I~\af{,}~\aof{ğ”»[~\ab{ğ’œ}~\ab i~]} of the domains of the algebras in \ab{ğ’œ}, and
whose operations are those arising from pointwise interpretation in the obvious way: if
\ab{f} is a \ab J-ary operation symbol and if
\ab a~:~\af{Î }~\ab i~ê‰~\ab I~\af{,}~\ab J~\as{â†’}~\aof{ğ”»[~\ab{ğ’œ}~\ab i~]} is, for each
\ab i~:~\ab I, a \ab J-tuple of elements of the domain \aof{ğ”»[~\ab{ğ’œ}~\ab i~]}, then
we define the interpretation of \ab f in \af{â¨…}~\ab{ğ’œ} by\\[-2mm]

(\ab{f}~\af{Ì‚}~\af{â¨…}~\ab{ğ’œ}) \ab a := \as{Î»}~(\ab i~:~\ab I)~\as{â†’}
(\ab{f}~\af{Ì‚}~\ab{ğ’œ}~\ab i)(\ab{a}~\ab i).\\[8pt]
Here is the formal definition of the product algebra type in \agda.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="32295" href="Function.Bundles.html#1938" class="Field">cong</a> <a id="32300" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="32301" href="Demos.HSP.html#24654" class="Field">Interp</a> <a id="32308" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="32309" href="Demos.HSP.html#31748" class="Function">â¨…</a> <a id="32311" href="Demos.HSP.html#32311" class="Bound">ğ’œ</a><a id="32312" class="Symbol">))</a> <a id="32315" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="32316" href="Agda.Builtin.Equality.html#208" class="InductiveConstructor">â‰¡.refl</a> <a id="32323" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="32325" href="Demos.HSP.html#32325" class="Bound">f=g</a> <a id="32329" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="32331" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="32333" class="Symbol">Î»</a> <a id="32335" href="Demos.HSP.html#32335" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="32337" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="32339" href="Function.Bundles.html#1938" class="Field">cong</a> <a id="32344" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="32345" href="Demos.HSP.html#24654" class="Field">Interp</a> <a id="32352" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="32353" href="Demos.HSP.html#32311" class="Bound">ğ’œ</a> <a id="32355" href="Demos.HSP.html#32335" class="Bound">i</a><a id="32356" class="Symbol">))</a> <a id="32359" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="32360" href="Agda.Builtin.Equality.html#208" class="InductiveConstructor">â‰¡.refl</a> <a id="32367" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="32369" href="Function.Base.html#1554" class="Function">flip</a> <a id="32374" href="Demos.HSP.html#32325" class="Bound">f=g</a> <a id="32378" href="Demos.HSP.html#32335" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="32380" class="Symbol">)</a>

</pre>
\noindent Evidently, the carrier of the product algebra type is indeed the (dependent)
product of the carriers in the indexed family. The rest of the definitions are the ``pointwise''
versions of the underlying ones.

%% -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
%\subsection{Homomorphisms}\label{homomorphisms}
\subsection{Structure preserving maps and isomorphism}\label{homomorphisms}
Throughout the rest of the paper, unless stated otherwise, \ab{ğ‘¨} and \ab{ğ‘©}
will denote \ab{ğ‘†}-algebras inhabiting the types \af{Algebra} \ab{Î±} \ab{Ïáµƒ} and
\af{Algebra} \ab{Î²} \ab{Ïáµ‡}, respectively.

A \defn{homomorphism} (or ``hom'') from
\ab{ğ‘¨} to \ab{ğ‘©} is a setoid function \ab{h}~:~\aof{ğ”»[~\ab{ğ‘¨}~]} \aor{âŸ¶} \aof{ğ”»[~\ab{ğ‘©}~]}
that is \defn{compatible} with all basic operations; that is, for
every operation symbol \ab{f} : \af{âˆ£~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ£} and all tuples
\ab{a} : \af{âˆ¥~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ¥}~\ab{f} \as{â†’} \aof{ğ•Œ[~\ab{ğ‘¨}~]}, we have \ab{h} \aofld{âŸ¨\$âŸ©}
(\ab{f}~\af{Ì‚}~\ab{ğ‘¨}) \ab{a} \af{â‰ˆ}
(\ab{f}~\af{Ì‚}~\ab{ğ‘©}) \as{Î»} \ab x \as{â†’} \ab h \AgdaOperator{\AgdaField{âŸ¨\$âŸ©}} (\ab a \ab x).

It is convenient to first formalize ``compatible'' (\af{compatible-map-op}),
representing the assertion that a given setoid function
\ab{h}~:~\aof{ğ”»[~\ab{ğ‘¨}~]} \aor{âŸ¶} \aof{ğ”»[~\ab{ğ‘©}~]} commutes with a given
operation symbol \ab{f}, and then generalize over operation symbols
to yield the type (\af{compatible-map}) of compatible maps from (the domain of)
\ab{ğ‘¨} to (the domain of) \ab{ğ‘©}.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="33913" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="33920" href="Demos.HSP.html#33920" class="Module">_</a> <a id="33922" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="33923" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="33925" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="33927" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="33935" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="33937" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a><a id="33939" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="33941" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="33943" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="33945" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="33953" href="Demos.HSP.html#9445" class="Generalizable">Î²</a> <a id="33955" href="Demos.HSP.html#9447" class="Generalizable">Ïáµ‡</a><a id="33957" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="33959" class="Keyword">where</a>

 <a id="33967" href="Demos.HSP.html#33967" class="Function">compatible-map-op</a> <a id="33985" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="33987" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="33988" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="33991" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="33993" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a> <a id="33995" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="33997" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="34000" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="34002" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a><a id="34003" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="34005" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="34007" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a> <a id="34009" href="Demos.HSP.html#7245" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a> <a id="34011" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a> <a id="34013" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="34015" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="34020" class="Symbol">_</a>
 <a id="34023" href="Demos.HSP.html#33967" class="Function">compatible-map-op</a> <a id="34041" href="Demos.HSP.html#34041" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="34043" href="Demos.HSP.html#34043" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="34045" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="34047" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="34049" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="34050" href="Demos.HSP.html#34050" class="Bound">a</a><a id="34051" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="34053" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="34055" href="Demos.HSP.html#34041" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="34057" href="Demos.HSP.html#8608" class="Field Operator">âŸ¨$âŸ©</a> <a id="34061" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="34062" href="Demos.HSP.html#34043" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="34064" href="Demos.HSP.html#25612" class="Function Operator">Ì‚</a> <a id="34066" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a><a id="34067" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="34069" href="Demos.HSP.html#34050" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="34071" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1098" class="Function Operator">â‰ˆ</a> <a id="34073" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="34074" href="Demos.HSP.html#34043" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="34076" href="Demos.HSP.html#25612" class="Function Operator">Ì‚</a> <a id="34078" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a><a id="34079" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="34081" class="Symbol">Î»</a> <a id="34083" href="Demos.HSP.html#34083" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="34085" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="34087" href="Demos.HSP.html#34041" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="34089" href="Demos.HSP.html#8608" class="Field Operator">âŸ¨$âŸ©</a> <a id="34093" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="34094" href="Demos.HSP.html#34050" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="34096" href="Demos.HSP.html#34083" class="Bound">x</a><a id="34097" class="Symbol">)</a>
  <a id="34101" class="Keyword">where</a> <a id="34107" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="34112" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1009" class="Module">Setoid</a> <a id="34119" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="34122" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="34124" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a> <a id="34126" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="34132" class="Symbol">(</a> <a id="34134" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1098" class="Field Operator">_â‰ˆ_</a> <a id="34138" class="Symbol">)</a>

 <a id="34142" href="Demos.HSP.html#34142" class="Function">compatible-map</a> <a id="34157" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="34159" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="34160" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="34163" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="34165" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a> <a id="34167" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="34169" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="34172" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="34174" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a><a id="34175" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="34177" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="34179" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="34184" class="Symbol">_</a>
 <a id="34187" href="Demos.HSP.html#34142" class="Function">compatible-map</a> <a id="34202" href="Demos.HSP.html#34202" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="34204" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="34206" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="34208" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="34209" href="Demos.HSP.html#34209" class="Bound">f</a><a id="34210" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="34212" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="34214" href="Demos.HSP.html#33967" class="Function">compatible-map-op</a> <a id="34232" href="Demos.HSP.html#34202" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="34234" href="Demos.HSP.html#34209" class="Bound">f</a>

</pre>
Using these we define the property (\ar{IsHom}) of being a homomorphism, and
finally the type (\af{hom}) of homomorphisms from \ab{ğ‘¨} to \ab{ğ‘©}.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="34409" class="Keyword">record</a> <a id="34416" href="Demos.HSP.html#34416" class="Record">IsHom</a> <a id="34422" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="34423" href="Demos.HSP.html#34423" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="34425" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="34427" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="34430" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="34432" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a> <a id="34434" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="34436" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="34439" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="34441" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a><a id="34442" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="34444" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="34446" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="34451" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="34452" href="Demos.HSP.html#7259" class="Bound">ğ“</a> <a id="34454" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="34456" href="Demos.HSP.html#7261" class="Bound">ğ“¥</a> <a id="34458" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="34460" href="Demos.HSP.html#33935" class="Bound">Î±</a> <a id="34462" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="34464" href="Demos.HSP.html#33955" class="Bound">Ïáµ‡</a><a id="34466" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="34468" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="34476" class="Keyword">constructor</a>  <a id="34489" href="Demos.HSP.html#34489" class="InductiveConstructor">mkhom</a>
  <a id="34497" class="Keyword">field</a>        <a id="34510" href="Demos.HSP.html#34510" class="Field">compatible</a> <a id="34521" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="34523" href="Demos.HSP.html#34142" class="Function">compatible-map</a> <a id="34538" href="Demos.HSP.html#34423" class="Bound">h</a>

 <a id="34542" href="Demos.HSP.html#34542" class="Function">hom</a> <a id="34546" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="34548" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="34553" class="Symbol">_</a>
 <a id="34556" href="Demos.HSP.html#34542" class="Function">hom</a> <a id="34560" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="34562" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#166" class="Record">Î£</a> <a id="34564" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="34565" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a>Â <a id="34568" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="34570" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a> <a id="34572" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="34574" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="34577" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="34579" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a><a id="34580" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="34582" href="Demos.HSP.html#34416" class="Record">IsHom</a>

</pre>
Thus, an inhabitant of \af{hom} is a pair (\ab h , \ab p) consisting of
a setoid function \ab h, from the domain of \ab{ğ‘¨} to that of \ab{ğ‘©}, along with
a proof \ab p that \ab h is a homomorphism.

A \defn{monomorphism} (resp. \defn{epimorphism}) is an injective (resp. surjective)
homomorphism. The \agdaalgebras library defines predicates \ar{IsMon} and \ar{IsEpi} for these,
as well as \af{mon} and \af{epi} for the corresponding types.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="35056" class="Keyword">record</a> <a id="35063" href="Demos.HSP.html#35063" class="Record">IsMon</a> <a id="35069" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="35070" href="Demos.HSP.html#35070" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="35072" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="35074" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="35077" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="35079" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a> <a id="35081" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="35083" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="35086" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="35088" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a><a id="35089" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="35091" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="35093" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="35098" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="35099" href="Demos.HSP.html#7259" class="Bound">ğ“</a> <a id="35101" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="35103" href="Demos.HSP.html#7261" class="Bound">ğ“¥</a> <a id="35105" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="35107" href="Demos.HSP.html#33935" class="Bound">Î±</a> <a id="35109" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="35111" href="Demos.HSP.html#33937" class="Bound">Ïáµƒ</a> <a id="35114" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="35116" href="Demos.HSP.html#33955" class="Bound">Ïáµ‡</a><a id="35118" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="35120" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="35128" class="Keyword">field</a>  <a id="35135" href="Demos.HSP.html#35135" class="Field">isHom</a> <a id="35141" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="35143" href="Demos.HSP.html#34416" class="Record">IsHom</a> <a id="35149" href="Demos.HSP.html#35070" class="Bound">h</a>

  <a id="35190" href="Demos.HSP.html#35190" class="Function">HomReduct</a> <a id="35200" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="35202" href="Demos.HSP.html#34542" class="Function">hom</a>
  <a id="35208" href="Demos.HSP.html#35190" class="Function">HomReduct</a> <a id="35218" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="35220" href="Demos.HSP.html#35070" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="35222" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="35224" href="Demos.HSP.html#35135" class="Field">isHom</a>

 <a id="35232" href="Demos.HSP.html#35232" class="Function">mon</a> <a id="35236" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="35238" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="35243" class="Symbol">_</a>
 <a id="35246" href="Demos.HSP.html#35232" class="Function">mon</a> <a id="35250" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="35252" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#166" class="Record">Î£</a> <a id="35254" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="35255" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="35258" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="35260" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a> <a id="35262" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="35264" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="35267" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="35269" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a><a id="35270" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="35272" href="Demos.HSP.html#35063" class="Record">IsMon</a>

</pre>
\noindent As with \af{hom}, the type \af{mon} is a dependent product type; each inhabitant is a pair
consisting of a setoid function, say, \ab h, along with a proof that \ab h is a monomorphism.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="35501" class="Keyword">record</a> <a id="35508" href="Demos.HSP.html#35508" class="Record">IsEpi</a> <a id="35514" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="35515" href="Demos.HSP.html#35515" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="35517" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="35519" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="35522" href="Demos.HSP.html#33923" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="35524" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a> <a id="35526" href="Demos.HSP.html#8506" class="Record Operator">âŸ¶</a> <a id="35528" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">ğ”»[</a> <a id="35531" href="Demos.HSP.html#33941" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="35533" href="Demos.HSP.html#25501" class="Function Operator">]</a><a id="35534" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="35536" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="35538" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="35543" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="35544" href="Demos.HSP.html#7259" class="Bound">ğ“</a> <a id="35546" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="35548" href="Demos.HSP.html#7261" class="Bound">ğ“¥</a> <a id="35550" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="35552" href="Demos.HSP.html#33935" class="Bound">Î±</a> <a id="35554" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="35556" href="Demos.HSP.html#33953" class="Bound">Î²</a> <a id="35558" href="Agda.Primitive.html#810" class="Primitive Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="35560" href="Demos.HSP.html#33955" class="Bound">Ïáµ‡</a><a id="35562" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="35564" class="Keyword">where</a>

\ifshort\else
Here are two utilities that are useful for translating between types.

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\fi

\paragraph*{Composition of homomorphisms}
The composition of homomorphisms is again a homomorphism, and similarly for epimorphisms and monomorphisms.
\ifshort
The proofs of these facts are straightforward so we omit them, but give them the names
\af{âˆ˜-hom} and \af{âˆ˜-epi} so we can refer to them below.
\else

<pre class="Agda">

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\paragraph*{Universe lifting of homomorphisms}
Here we define the identity homomorphism for setoid algebras. Then we prove that the
operations of lifting and lowering of a setoid algebra are homomorphisms.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="ğ’¾ğ’¹"></a><a id="37766" href="Demos.HSP.html#37766" class="Function">ğ’¾ğ’¹</a> <a id="37769" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="37771" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="37772" href="Demos.HSP.html#37772" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="37774" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="37776" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="37784" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="37786" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a><a id="37788" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="37790" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="37792" href="Demos.HSP.html#34542" class="Function">hom</a> <a id="37796" href="Demos.HSP.html#37772" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="37798" href="Demos.HSP.html#37772" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a>
<a id="37800" href="Demos.HSP.html#37766" class="Function">ğ’¾ğ’¹</a> <a id="37803" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="37804" class="Argument">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="37806" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="37808" href="Demos.HSP.html#37808" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a><a id="37809" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="37811" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="37813" href="Demos.HSP.html#12839" class="Function">ğ‘–ğ‘‘</a> <a id="37816" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="37818" href="Demos.HSP.html#34489" class="InductiveConstructor">mkhom</a> <a id="37824" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="37825" href="Relation.Binary.Structures.html#1646" class="Function">reflexive</a> <a id="37835" href="Agda.Builtin.Equality.html#208" class="InductiveConstructor">â‰¡.refl</a><a id="37841" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="37843" class="Keyword">where</a> <a id="37849" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="37854" href="Relation.Binary.Bundles.html#1009" class="Module">Setoid</a> <a id="37861" class="Symbol">(</a> <a id="37863" href="Demos.HSP.html#24625" class="Field">Domain</a> <a id="37870" href="Demos.HSP.html#37808" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="37872" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="37874" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="37880" class="Symbol">(</a> <a id="37882" href="Relation.Binary.Structures.html#1646" class="Function">reflexive</a> <a id="37892" class="Symbol">)</a>

\paragraph*{Homomorphisms of product algebras}
Suppose we have an algebra \ab{ğ‘¨}, a type \ab I : \ap{Type} \ab{ğ“˜}, and a family \ab{â„¬} :
\ab I \as{â†’} \ar{Algebra} \ab{Î²} \ab{Ïáµ‡} of algebras.
We sometimes refer to the inhabitants of \ab{I} as \emph{indices}, and call \ab{â„¬} an
\defn{indexed family of algebras}. If in addition we have a family \ab{ğ’½} : (\ab i : \ab
I) â†’ \af{hom} \ab{ğ‘¨} (\ab{â„¬} \ab i) of homomorphisms, then we can construct a homomorphism
from \ab{ğ‘¨} to the product \af{â¨…} \ab{â„¬} in the natural way.  We codify the latter in
dependent type theory as follows.

\fi

Two structures are \defn{isomorphic} provided there are homomorphisms from each to the
other that compose to the identity. We define the following record type to represent this concept.
%We represent this notion by the type \ar{\au{}â‰…\au{}}.
\ifshort
\else
Note that the definition, shown below, includes a proof of the fact that the maps \afld{to} and
\afld{from} are bijective, which makes this fact more accessible.
\fi

\ifshort
The \agdaalgebras library also includes formal proof that the \afld{to} and \afld{from} maps are bijections and that \ar{\au{}â‰…\au{}} is an equivalence relation, but we suppress these details.
\else
<pre class="Agda">

<a id="42228" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="42233" href="Demos.HSP.html#41315" class="Module Operator">_â‰…_</a>

It is easy to prove that \ar{\au{}â‰…\au{}} is an equivalence relation, as follows.

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\paragraph*{Homomorphic images}
We have found that a useful way to encode the concept of \emph{homomorphic image}
is to produce a witness, that is, a surjective hom.  Thus we define the type of surjective homs
and also record the fact that an algebra is its own homomorphic image via the identity
hom.\footnote{Here and elsewhere we use the shorthand \af{ov}~\ab{Î±} := \ab{ğ’ª}
\ap{âŠ”} \ab{ğ’±} \ap{âŠ”} \ab{Î±}, for any level \ab{Î±}.}

\paragraph*{Factorization of homomorphisms}
Another theorem in the \agdaalgebras library, called \af{HomFactor}, formalizes the following factorization result: if \ab g : \af{hom}
\ab{ğ‘¨} \ab{ğ‘©}, \ab h : \af{hom} \ab{ğ‘¨} \ab{ğ‘ª}, \ab h is surjective, and \af{ker} \ab h
\aof{âŠ†} \af{ker} \ab g, then there exists \ab{Ï†} : \af{hom} \ab{ğ‘ª} \ab{ğ‘©} such that \ab g = \ab{Ï†} \aof{âˆ˜} \ab h.
A special case of this result that we use below is the fact that the setoid function factorization we saw above %---\ab f = %: \ab A \aor{âŸ¶} \ab B factors as a surjective map
%\ab{fromIm} \aof{âˆ˜} \ab{toIm}---% : \ab A \aor{âŸ¶} \ab{Im} \ab f followed by an injective map \ab{fromIm} : \ab{Im} \ab f \aor{âŸ¶} \ab B.
lifts to factorization of homomorphisms. Moreover, we associate a homomorphism \ab h with its image---which is (the domain of) a subalgebra of the codomain of \ab h---using the function \ab{HomIm} defined below.\footnote{The definition of \ab{HomIm} was provided by an anonymous referee; it is indeed simpler than the general \af{HomFactor} theorem.}

  <a id="45856" href="Relation.Binary.Reasoning.Base.Single.html#1916" class="Function Operator">begin</a>
      <a id="45868" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a> <a id="45870" href="Demos.HSP.html#45814" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="45872" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a>  <a id="45875" href="Demos.HSP.html#8608" class="Field Operator">âŸ¨$âŸ©</a>         <a id="45887" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="45888" href="Demos.HSP.html#24654" class="Field">Interp</a> <a id="45895" href="Demos.HSP.html#45640" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a>  <a id="45898" href="Demos.HSP.html#8608" class="Field Operator">âŸ¨$âŸ©</a> <a id="45902" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="45903" href="Demos.HSP.html#45819" class="Bound">x1</a> <a id="45906" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="45908" href="Demos.HSP.html#45824" class="Bound">x2</a><a id="45910" class="Symbol">))</a>  <a id="45914" href="Relation.Binary.Reasoning.Setoid.html#1052" class="Function">â‰ˆâŸ¨</a> <a id="45917" href="Demos.HSP.html#46287" class="Function">h-compatible</a>                  <a id="45947" href="Relation.Binary.Reasoning.Setoid.html#1052" class="Function">âŸ©</a>

%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Lift-Alg is an algebraic invariant}\label{sec:lift-alg}
The \af{Lift-Alg} operation neatly resolves the technical problem of
universe non-cumulativity because isomorphism classes of algebras are closed under \af{Lift-Alg}.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="46844" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="46851" href="Demos.HSP.html#46851" class="Module">_</a> <a id="46853" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="46854" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="46856" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="46858" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="46866" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="46868" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a><a id="46870" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="46872" href="Demos.HSP.html#46872" class="Bound">â„“</a> <a id="46874" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="46876" href="Agda.Primitive.html#597" class="Postulate">Level</a><a id="46881" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="46883" class="Keyword">where</a>
 <a id="46890" href="Demos.HSP.html#46890" class="Function">Lift-â‰…Ë¡</a> <a id="46898" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="46900" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="46902" href="Demos.HSP.html#41315" class="Record Operator">â‰…</a> <a id="46904" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="46905" href="Demos.HSP.html#28543" class="Function">Lift-AlgË¡</a> <a id="46915" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="46917" href="Demos.HSP.html#46872" class="Bound">â„“</a><a id="46918" class="Symbol">)</a>
 <a id="46921" href="Demos.HSP.html#46890" class="Function">Lift-â‰…Ë¡</a> <a id="46929" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="46931" href="Demos.HSP.html#41374" class="InductiveConstructor">mkiso</a> <a id="46937" href="Demos.HSP.html#38237" class="Function">ToLiftË¡</a> <a id="46945" href="Demos.HSP.html#38341" class="Function">FromLiftË¡</a> <a id="46955" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="46956" href="Demos.HSP.html#38437" class="Function">ToFromLiftË¡</a><a id="46967" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="46968" class="Argument">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="46970" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="46972" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a><a id="46973" class="Symbol">})</a> <a id="46976" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="46977" href="Demos.HSP.html#38526" class="Function">FromToLiftË¡</a><a id="46988" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="46989" class="Argument">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="46991" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="46993" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a><a id="46994" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="46996" href="Demos.HSP.html#46872" class="Bound">â„“</a><a id="46997" class="Symbol">})</a>
 <a id="47001" href="Demos.HSP.html#47001" class="Function">Lift-â‰…Ê³</a> <a id="47009" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="47011" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="47013" href="Demos.HSP.html#41315" class="Record Operator">â‰…</a> <a id="47015" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="47016" href="Demos.HSP.html#28938" class="Function">Lift-AlgÊ³</a> <a id="47026" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="47028" href="Demos.HSP.html#46872" class="Bound">â„“</a><a id="47029" class="Symbol">)</a>
 <a id="47032" href="Demos.HSP.html#47001" class="Function">Lift-â‰…Ê³</a> <a id="47040" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="47042" href="Demos.HSP.html#41374" class="InductiveConstructor">mkiso</a> <a id="47048" href="Demos.HSP.html#38614" class="Function">ToLiftÊ³</a> <a id="47056" href="Demos.HSP.html#38725" class="Function">FromLiftÊ³</a> <a id="47066" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="47067" href="Demos.HSP.html#38821" class="Function">ToFromLiftÊ³</a><a id="47078" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="47079" class="Argument">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="47081" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="47083" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a><a id="47084" class="Symbol">})</a> <a id="47087" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="47088" href="Demos.HSP.html#38914" class="Function">FromToLiftÊ³</a><a id="47099" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="47100" class="Argument">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="47102" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="47104" href="Demos.HSP.html#46854" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a><a id="47105" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="47107" href="Demos.HSP.html#46872" class="Bound">â„“</a><a id="47108" class="Symbol">})</a>

<a id="47176" href="Demos.HSP.html#47112" class="Function">Lift-â‰…</a> <a id="47183" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="47185" href="Demos.HSP.html#42571" class="Function">â‰…-trans</a> <a id="47193" href="Demos.HSP.html#46890" class="Function">Lift-â‰…Ë¡</a> <a id="47201" href="Demos.HSP.html#47001" class="Function">Lift-â‰…Ê³</a>
</pre>
%% -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Subalgebras}
\label{subalgebras}
%Given \ab{ğ‘†}-algebras \ab{ğ‘¨} and \ab{ğ‘©},
We say that \ab{ğ‘¨} is a \defn{subalgebra} of
\ab{ğ‘©} and write \ab{ğ‘¨}~\aof{â‰¤}~\ab{ğ‘©} just in case \ab{ğ‘¨} can be \emph{homomorphically
embedded} in \ab{ğ‘©}; in other terms, \ab{ğ‘¨}~\aof{â‰¤}~\ab{ğ‘©} iff there exists an injective
hom from \ab{ğ‘¨} to \ab{ğ‘©}.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="_â‰¤_"></a><a id="47660" href="Demos.HSP.html#47660" class="Function Operator">_â‰¤_</a> <a id="47664" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="47666" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="47674" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="47676" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a> <a id="47679" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="47681" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="47689" href="Demos.HSP.html#9445" class="Generalizable">Î²</a> <a id="47691" href="Demos.HSP.html#9447" class="Generalizable">Ïáµ‡</a> <a id="47694" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="47696" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="47701" class="Symbol">_</a>
<a id="47703" href="Demos.HSP.html#47703" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="47705" href="Demos.HSP.html#47660" class="Function Operator">â‰¤</a> <a id="47707" href="Demos.HSP.html#47707" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="47709" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="47711" href="Data.Product.html#916" class="Function">Î£[</a> <a id="47714" href="Demos.HSP.html#47714" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="47716" href="Data.Product.html#916" class="Function">âˆˆ</a> <a id="47718" href="Demos.HSP.html#34542" class="Function">hom</a> <a id="47722" href="Demos.HSP.html#47703" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="47724" href="Demos.HSP.html#47707" class="Bound">ğ‘©</a> <a id="47726" href="Data.Product.html#916" class="Function">]</a> <a id="47728" href="Demos.HSP.html#15539" class="Function">IsInjective</a> <a id="47740" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a> <a id="47742" href="Demos.HSP.html#47714" class="Bound">h</a> <a id="47744" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a>

</pre>
The subalgebra relation is reflexive, by the identity monomorphism (and transitive by composition of monomorphisms, hence, a \defn{preorder}, though we won't need this fact here).

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="â‰¤-reflexive"></a><a id="47953" href="Demos.HSP.html#47953" class="Function">â‰¤-reflexive</a>   <a id="47967" class="Symbol">:</a>  <a id="47970" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="47971" href="Demos.HSP.html#47971" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="47973" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="47975" href="Demos.HSP.html#24569" class="Record">Algebra</a> <a id="47983" href="Demos.HSP.html#9440" class="Generalizable">Î±</a> <a id="47985" href="Demos.HSP.html#9442" class="Generalizable">Ïáµƒ</a><a id="47987" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="47989" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="47991" href="Demos.HSP.html#47971" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a> <a id="47993" href="Demos.HSP.html#47660" class="Function Operator">â‰¤</a> <a id="47995" href="Demos.HSP.html#47971" class="Bound">ğ‘¨</a>
<a id="47997" href="Demos.HSP.html#47953" class="Function">â‰¤-reflexive</a> <a id="48009" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="48011" href="Demos.HSP.html#37766" class="Function">ğ’¾ğ’¹</a> <a id="48014" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="48016" href="Function.Base.html#615" class="Function">id</a>

</pre>
%â‰¤-transitive  :  {ğ‘¨ : Algebra Î± Ïáµƒ}{ğ‘© : Algebra Î² Ïáµ‡}{ğ‘ª : Algebra Î³ Ïá¶œ} â†’ ğ‘¨ â‰¤ ğ‘© â†’ ğ‘© â‰¤ ğ‘ª â†’ ğ‘¨ â‰¤ ğ‘ª
%â‰¤-transitive ( f , finj ) ( g , ginj ) = (âˆ˜-hom f g ) , âˆ˜-IsInjective âˆ£ f âˆ£ âˆ£ g âˆ£ finj ginj
If
\ab{ğ’œ} : \ab I â†’ \af{Algebra} \ab{Î±} \ab{Ïáµƒ},
\ab{â„¬} : \ab I â†’ \af{Algebra} \ab{Î²} \ab{Ïáµ‡} (families of \ab{ğ‘†}-algebras) and if
\ab{â„¬} \ab i \af{â‰¤} \ab{ğ’œ} \ab i for all \ab i~:~\ab I, then \af{â¨…} \ab{â„¬} is a subalgebra
of \af{â¨…} \ab{ğ’œ}. Below we will use \af{â¨…-â‰¤} to denote this fact.

We conclude this section with an easy fact that will be useful later;
it simply converts a monomorphism into a proof of a subalgebra relationship.
%The first converts a monomorphism to a subalgebra witness while the second is an algebraic invariance property of \aof{â‰¤}.

%% -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

\subsection{Terms}
\label{terms}
Fix a signature \ab{ğ‘†} and let \ab X denote an arbitrary nonempty collection of variable
symbols. Such a collection is called a \defn{context}.
Assume the symbols in \ab X are distinct from the operation symbols of
\ab{ğ‘†}, that is \ab X \aof{âˆ©} \aof{âˆ£} \ab{ğ‘†} \aof{âˆ£} = âˆ….
A \defn{word} in the language of \ab{ğ‘†} is a finite sequence of members of \ab X \aof{âˆª}
\aof{âˆ£~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ£}. We denote the concatenation of such sequences by simple juxtaposition.
Let \ab{Sâ‚€} denote the set of nullary operation symbols of \ab{ğ‘†}. We define by induction
on \textit{n} the sets \ab{ğ‘‡â‚™} of \emph{words} over \ab X \aof{âˆª} \aof{âˆ£~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ£} as
follows: %(cf.~\cite[Def. 4.19]{Bergman:2012}):
\ab{ğ‘‡â‚€} := \ab X \aof{âˆª} \ab{Sâ‚€} and
\ab{ğ‘‡â‚™â‚Šâ‚} := \ab{ğ‘‡â‚™} \aof{âˆª} \ab{ğ’¯â‚™}, where \ab{ğ’¯â‚™} is the collection of all \ab f \ab t
such that \ab f : \aof{âˆ£~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ£} and \ab t : \aof{âˆ¥~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ¥} \ab f \as{â†’}
\ab{ğ‘‡â‚™}.
\ifshort\else
(Recall, \aof{âˆ¥~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ¥} \ab f is the arity of the operation symbol \ab f.)
\fi
An \ab{ğ‘†}-\defn{term} is a term in the language of \ab{ğ‘†} and the collection of all
\ab{ğ‘†}-\defn{terms} in the context \ab X is \Term{X} := \aof{â‹ƒâ‚™} \ab{ğ‘‡â‚™}.

In type theory, this translates to two cases: variable injection and applying an
operation symbol to a tuple of terms. This represents each term as a tree
with an operation symbol at each \aic{node} and a variable symbol at each leaf \aic{â„Š};
hence the constructor names (\aic{â„Š} for ``generator'' and \aic{node} for ``node'') in the
following inductively defined type.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="50760" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="Term"></a><a id="50765" href="Demos.HSP.html#50765" class="Datatype">Term</a> <a id="50770" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="50771" href="Demos.HSP.html#50771" class="Bound">X</a> <a id="50773" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="50775" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="50780" href="Demos.HSP.html#9462" class="Generalizable">Ï‡</a><a id="50781" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="50783" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="50785" href="Demos.HSP.html#8241" class="Primitive">Type</a> <a id="50790" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="50791" href="Demos.HSP.html#43706" class="Function">ov</a> <a id="50794" href="Demos.HSP.html#50780" class="Bound">Ï‡</a><a id="50795" class="Symbol">)</a>  <a id="50798" class="Keyword">where</a>
 <a id="Term.â„Š"></a><a id="50805" href="Demos.HSP.html#50805" class="InductiveConstructor">â„Š</a> <a id="50807" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="50809" href="Demos.HSP.html#50771" class="Bound">X</a> <a id="50811" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="50813" href="Demos.HSP.html#50765" class="Datatype">Term</a> <a id="50818" href="Demos.HSP.html#50771" class="Bound">X</a>
 <a id="Term.node"></a><a id="50821" href="Demos.HSP.html#50821" class="InductiveConstructor">node</a> <a id="50826" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="50828" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="50829" href="Demos.HSP.html#50829" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="50831" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="50833" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a> <a id="50835" href="Demos.HSP.html#7245" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a> <a id="50837" href="Demos.HSP.html#10364" class="Function Operator">âˆ£</a><a id="50838" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="50840" href="Demos.HSP.html#50840" class="Bound">t</a> <a id="50842" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="50844" href="Demos.HSP.html#10401" class="Function Operator">âˆ¥</a> <a id="50846" href="Demos.HSP.html#7245" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a> <a id="50848" href="Demos.HSP.html#10401" class="Function Operator">âˆ¥</a> <a id="50850" href="Demos.HSP.html#50829" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="50852" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="50854" href="Demos.HSP.html#50765" class="Datatype">Term</a> <a id="50859" href="Demos.HSP.html#50771" class="Bound">X</a><a id="50860" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="50862" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="50864" href="Demos.HSP.html#50765" class="Datatype">Term</a> <a id="50869" href="Demos.HSP.html#50771" class="Bound">X</a>
</pre>
%% -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
\paragraph*{The term algebra}
We enrich the \ad{Term} type to a setoid of  \ab{ğ‘†}-terms, which will ultimately
be the domain of an algebra, called the \emph{term algebra in the signature} \ab{ğ‘†}.
For this we need an equivalence relation on terms.

<pre class="Agda">

</pre>
\fi

For a given signature \ab{ğ‘†} and context \ab X,
%if the type \Term{X} is nonempty (equivalently, if \ab X or
%\aof{âˆ£~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ£} is nonempty), then
we define the algebra \T{X}, known as the \defn{term algebra in} \ab{ğ‘†} \defn{over} \ab
X.
%Terms are viewed as acting on other terms, so both
%the elements of the domain of \T{X}
%and its basic operations are terms themselves.
The domain of \T{X} is \Term{X} and, for each operation symbol \ab
f : \aof{âˆ£~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ£}, we define \ab f~\aof{Ì‚}~\T{X} to be the operation which maps
each tuple \ab t : \aof{âˆ¥~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ¥} \ab f \as{â†’} \Term{X} of terms to the formal
term \ab f \ab t.
%We let \T{X} denote the term algebra in \ab{ğ‘†} over \ab X; it has universe \Term{X} and
%operations \ab f \aof{Ì‚} (\T{X}), one for each symbol \ab f in \aof{âˆ£~\ab{ğ‘†}~âˆ£}.
